  <raw>Region Digest



DUCKTOWN, TENN.
Heavy releases expected on Ocoee
Heavy water releases this weekend could make the Ocoee River unsafe for swimmers and waders in the pools below the Whitewater Center, officials said.
Center manager Sherry Hicks said TVA will release as much as 1,000 cubic feet per second from the Blue Ridge Reservoir. River levels can rise in just five minutes without warning, she said.

State rangers have said several people have been trapped on rocks during recent releases, but so far no injuries have been reported.
TRACY CITY, TENN.
Theater hosting symposium, film
The Alma Mater Theater here is presenting a symposium on Andy Goldsworthy's film, "Rivers and Tides."
The Southeastern premier of the film will last through Sunday, said organizer Ed Russell. A speaker will give a presentation at 6:30 p.m. CDT before each showing, he said.
Mr. Goldsworthy is an environmental artist who uses sheep's wool, flowers and thorns as artistic materials. For more information, call (931) 592-5234.
RINGGOLD, GA.
Candidate steps up in commission race
Ringgold resident James Emberson, 67, a retired service manager for Provident Life Insurance Co., said he will seek the 3rd District Catoosa County Commission seat.
A special election has been called for Sept. 16 to fill the unexpired seat of County Commissioner Burke Hale, who died earlier this month. Qualifying begins July 28 and ends at noon July 30.
Mr. Emberson, a former Marine, has been a mentor at Ringgold Middle School for five years under the Partnership 2000 Program. He and his wife, Gail, have three sons and two grandchildren.
CLEVELAND, TENN.
Scholarship to honor Buckner
The son of Ralph Buckner has contributed $10,000 to the Cleveland State Community College Foundation to establish a scholarship for students pursuing careers in public safety.
Mr. Buckner was a funeral home operator in Cleveland for many years and was the city's police commissioner from 1974 to 1981.
The scholarship will be available for students from Bradley, Polk and McMinn counties.
ATLANTA
Courthouse named after prosecutor
The Fulton County Courthouse will carry the named of a man who prosecuted some of Atlanta's most famous murder cases in three decades as district attorney.
Lewis Slaton's cases included those of Wayne Williams, in the missing and murdered children saga of the 1980s, and Marcus Wayne Chenault, who killed the mother of the Rev. Martin Luther King Jr.
Slaton died last year at the age of 80. He was district attorney from 1965 to 1996.</raw>
